Extended Security Properties (CIA + AAA)

PropertyDefinitionThreatsControls
ConfidentialityInformation disclosed only to authorized partiesEavesdropping, data breaches, social engineeringEncryption, access controls, data classification
IntegrityInformation is accurate and unmodifiedTampering, man-in-the-middle, SQL injectionHashing, digital signatures, input validation
AvailabilitySystems accessible when neededDDoS, hardware failure, ransomwareRedundancy, backups, capacity planning
AuthenticationVerifying identity claimsCredential theft, phishing, brute forceMFA, strong passwords, biometrics
AuthorizationEnforcing access permissionsPrivilege escalation, broken access controlRBAC, ABAC, least privilege
AccountabilityTracking actions to individualsRepudiation, audit tamperingLogging, audit trails, non-repudiation

â”‚  â€¢ Always validate the signature                                            â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Check expiration (exp) and not-before (nbf)                              â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Verify issuer (iss) matches expected value                               â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Verify audience (aud) includes your service                              â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Use asymmetric algorithms (RS256, ES256) for distributed systems         â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Keep tokens short-lived (minutes, not days)                              â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Use HTTPS for all token transmission                                     â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Implement token revocation for sensitive operations                      â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Rotate signing keys periodically                                         â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚

â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Store sensitive data in JWT payload (it's not encrypted!)                â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Use the "none" algorithm                                                 â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Trust the alg header without validation                                  â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Store JWTs in localStorage (XSS vulnerable)                              â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Create tokens with very long expiration                                  â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Use weak or predictable signing keys                                     â”‚
â”‚  â€¢ Skip validation because "it's internal"                                  â”‚

â”‚  1. ALGORITHM CONFUSION                                                     â”‚
â”‚     Attack: Attacker changes alg from RS256 to HS256                        â”‚
â”‚             Uses public key as HMAC secret                                  â”‚
â”‚     Prevention: Explicitly specify allowed algorithms in validation         â”‚
â”‚                 Never accept "none" algorithm                               â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚  2. MISSING SIGNATURE VALIDATION                                            â”‚
â”‚     Attack: Attacker modifies payload, server doesn't verify signature      â”‚
â”‚     Prevention: Always verify signature before trusting claims              â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚  3. TOKEN LEAKAGE                                                           â”‚
â”‚     Attack: Token exposed via logs, URLs, or insecure storage               â”‚
â”‚     Prevention: Never log tokens, use secure storage, short TTL             â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚  4. WEAK SECRETS                                                            â”‚
â”‚     Attack: Brute force HMAC secret for HS256 tokens                        â”‚
â”‚     Prevention: Use strong, random secrets (256+ bits)                      â”‚
â”‚                 Prefer asymmetric algorithms                                â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚
â”‚  5. KID INJECTION                                                           â”‚
â”‚     Attack: Manipulate key ID (kid) to point to attacker's key              â”‚
â”‚     Prevention: Validate kid against allowlist of known keys                â”‚
â”‚                                                                             â”‚

â”‚  â”‚  Rate Limiting Strategies:                                          â”‚   â”‚
â”‚  â”‚                                                                     â”‚   â”‚
â”‚  â”‚  1. FIXED WINDOW                                                    â”‚   â”‚
â”‚  â”‚     100 requests per minute, resets at minute boundary              â”‚   â”‚
â”‚  â”‚     Simple but can allow burst at window boundaries                 â”‚   â”‚
â”‚  â”‚                                                                     â”‚   â”‚
â”‚  â”‚  2. SLIDING WINDOW                                                  â”‚   â”‚
â”‚  â”‚     100 requests in any rolling 60-second period                    â”‚   â”‚
â”‚  â”‚     Smoother rate limiting                                          â”‚   â”‚
â”‚  â”‚                                                                     â”‚   â”‚
â”‚  â”‚  3. TOKEN BUCKET                                                    â”‚   â”‚
â”‚  â”‚     Bucket fills with tokens at fixed rate                          â”‚   â”‚
â”‚  â”‚     Each request consumes a token                                   â”‚   â”‚
â”‚  â”‚     Allows controlled bursts                                        â”‚   â”‚
â”‚  â”‚                                                                     â”‚   â”‚
â”‚  â”‚  4. LEAKY BUCKET                                                    â”‚   â”‚
â”‚  â”‚     Requests processed at constant rate                             â”‚   â”‚
â”‚  â”‚     Excess requests queued or rejected                              â”‚   â”‚
